Part VI: Current Events
Chapter 11: End-Times Signs: 2026 Expanded
Analysis
Signs of the End Times: A Biblical and Current Events
Analysis
1. Introduction
Purpose
This study examines key biblical signs of the end times in light of current global events, using Scripture
alone as our interpretive framework. The Bible interprets the Bible—we allow God's Word to define its
own terms, establish its own patterns, and reveal its own meaning through the witness of multiple
passages.
As Jesus commanded: "Search the Scriptures; for in them ye think ye have eternal life: and they are
they which testify of me" (John 5:39). And as Isaiah declared: "To the law and to the testimony: if they
speak not according to this word, it is because there is no light in them" (Isaiah 8:20).
Overview of the Biblical Understanding of the Last Days
Scripture defines the "last days" as a period that began with Christ's first coming. The writer of
Hebrews states: "God, who at sundry times and in divers manners spake in time past unto the fathers by
the prophets, hath in these last days spoken unto us by his Son" (Hebrews 1:1-2). Peter, on the day of
Pentecost, declared that the outpouring of the Spirit fulfilled Joel's prophecy concerning the last days
(Acts 2:16-17, quoting Joel 2:28-32).
The apostle John confirmed this understanding: "Little children, it is the last time: and as ye have heard
that antichrist shall come, even now are there many antichrists; whereby we know that it is the last
time" (1 John 2:18).


---

Yet Scripture also reveals that the last days will intensify toward a climax. Paul wrote to Timothy:
"This know also, that in the last days perilous times shall come" (2 Timothy 3:1). Jesus Himself
provided specific signs to watch for, comparing them to birth pains that increase in frequency and
intensity: "All these are the beginning of sorrows" (Matthew 24:8)—the Greek word "sorrows" (Idin)
means birth pangs.
The principle of convergence appears in Christ's teaching: "So likewise ye, when ye shall see all these
things, know that it is near, even at the doors" (Matthew 24:33). Individual signs have appeared
throughout the church age, but the simultaneous convergence of multiple signs marks the approach of
the end.
2. The Persecution of Christians
Current Global Data
Nearly 400 million Christians face high to extreme persecution globally. Believers are killed,
imprisoned, and driven from their homes in record numbers across Africa, Asia, and the Middle East.
The church faces increasing restriction and hostility even in historically Christian nations.
What Scripture Declares
Jesus foretold persecution as normative:
"Then shall they deliver you up to be afflicted, and shall kill you: and ye shall be hated of all nations for
my name's sake" (Matthew 24:9).
"Remember the word that I said unto you, The servant is not greater than his lord. If they have
persecuted me, they will also persecute you" (John 15:20).
"These things I have spoken unto you, that in me ye might have peace. In the world ye shall have
tribulation: but be of good cheer; I have overcome the world" (John 16:33).
The pattern was established from the beginning:
Cain killed Abel because "his own works were evil, and his brother's righteous" (1 John 3:12). This
establishes the biblical pattern: the wicked persecute the righteous because righteousness condemns
wickedness.
Paul taught this as normative: "Yea, and all that will live godly in Christ Jesus shall suffer persecution"
(2 Timothy 3:12).
The book of Revelation reveals martyrdom throughout the church age:


---

"And when he had opened the fifth seal, I saw under the altar the souls of them that were slain for the
word of God, and for the testimony which they held: And they cried with a loud voice, saying, How
long, O Lord, holy and true, dost thou not judge and avenge our blood on them that dwell on the earth?
And white robes were given unto every one of them; and it was said unto them, that they should rest yet
for a little season, until their fellowservants also and their brethren, that should be killed as they were,
should be fulfilled" (Revelation 6:9-11).
This passage reveals: (1) martyrdom continues throughout history, (2) the martyrs cry out for justice,
(3) a specific number of martyrs must be completed before God's judgment falls.
The saints overcome through faithfulness:
"And they overcame him by the blood of the Lamb, and by the word of their testimony; and they loved
not their lives unto the death" (Revelation 12:11).
Scripture's interpretation of persecution:
Persecution is not defeat but victory. Christ Himself "endured the cross, despising the shame"
(Hebrews 12:2). The apostles rejoiced "that they were counted worthy to suffer shame for his name"
(Acts 5:41). James commands: "My brethren, count it all joy when ye fall into divers temptations"
(James 1:2). Peter writes: "Beloved, think it not strange concerning the fiery trial which is to try you, as
though some strange thing happened unto you: But rejoice, inasmuch as ye are partakers of Christ's
sufferings" (1 Peter 4:12-13).
The global scope of modern persecution—believers hated "of all nations"—aligns precisely with
Christ's prophecy.
3. Geopolitical Upheaval and the Middle East
Current Global Conflicts
Wars rage across multiple continents. The Middle East remains volatile, with Israel at the center of
regional conflict. Nations arm themselves at unprecedented rates. Economic instability and political
tension characterize international relations.
What Scripture Declares
Jesus prophesied wars and conflicts:
"And ye shall hear of wars and rumours of wars: see that ye be not troubled: for all these things must
come to pass, but the end is not yet. For nation shall rise against nation, and kingdom against kingdom:
and there shall be famines, and pestilences, and earthquakes, in divers places. All these are the
beginning of sorrows" (Matthew 24:6-8).


---

"And there shall be signs in the sun, and in the moon, and in the stars; and upon the earth distress of
nations, with perplexity; the sea and the waves roaring; Men's hearts failing them for fear, and for
looking after those things which are coming on the earth" (Luke 21:25-26).
The significance of Israel in Scripture:
God made an everlasting covenant with Abraham concerning the land: "And I will establish my
covenant between me and thee and thy seed after thee in their generations for an everlasting covenant,
to be a God unto thee, and to thy seed after thee. And I will give unto thee, and to thy seed after thee,
the land wherein thou art a stranger, all the land of Canaan, for an everlasting possession; and I will
be their God" (Genesis 17:7-8).
God promised to regather Israel from the nations: "For I will take you from among the heathen, and
gather you out of all countries, and will bring you into your own land" (Ezekiel 36:24).
"Thus saith the Lord GOD; Behold, I will take the children of Israel from among the heathen, whither
they be gone, and will gather them on every side, and bring them into their own land" (Ezekiel 37:21).
Ezekiel's vision of the valley of dry bones depicts Israel's restoration: "Then he said unto me, Son of
man, these bones are the whole house of Israel... Behold, O my people, I will open your graves, and
cause you to come up out of your graves, and bring you into the land of Israel" (Ezekiel 37:11-12).
Jerusalem's prophetic significance:
"Behold, I will make Jerusalem a cup of trembling unto all the people round about, when they shall be
in the siege both against Judah and against Jerusalem. And in that day will I make Jerusalem a
burdensome stone for all people: all that burden themselves with it shall be cut in pieces, though all the
people of the earth be gathered together against it" (Zechariah 12:2-3).
This prophecy declares that Jerusalem will become a source of contention for all nations—a condition
that did not exist for centuries while Israel was scattered but describes current geopolitical reality
precisely.
"And when ye shall see Jerusalem compassed with armies, then know that the desolation thereof is
nigh" (Luke 21:20).
The regathering precedes spiritual renewal:
Scripture reveals a two-stage restoration—first physical, then spiritual:
"For I will take you from among the heathen, and gather you out of all countries, and will bring you
into your own land. Then will I sprinkle clean water upon you, and ye shall be clean... A new heart also
will I give you, and a new spirit will I put within you" (Ezekiel 36:24-26).
The physical regathering (1948 and ongoing) precedes the spiritual transformation that Zechariah
prophesies: "And I will pour upon the house of David, and upon the inhabitants of Jerusalem, the spirit
of grace and of supplications: and they shall look upon me whom they have pierced, and they shall


---

mourn for him" (Zechariah 12:10).
Paul confirms Israel's future salvation: "And so all Israel shall be saved: as it is written, There shall
come out of Sion the Deliverer, and shall turn away ungodliness from Jacob" (Romans 11:26).
4. Moral and Societal Decay
Current Conditions
Western societies have undergone rapid moral transformation. Behaviors Scripture calls sin are now
celebrated. Biblical standards are rejected as bigotry. The family structure has deteriorated. Sexual
immorality is normalized across media and education.
What Scripture Declares
Paul's prophetic description of the last days:
"This know also, that in the last days perilous times shall come. For men shall be lovers of their own
selves, covetous, boasters, proud, blasphemers, disobedient to parents, unthankful, unholy, Without
natural affection, trucebreakers, false accusers, incontinent, fierce, despisers of those that are good,
Traitors, heady, highminded, lovers of pleasures more than lovers of God; Having a form of godliness,
but denying the power thereof: from such turn away" (2 Timothy 3:1-5).
Note the characteristics: - "Lovers of their own selves" — self-worship, narcissism - "Lovers of
pleasures more than lovers of God" — hedonism displacing worship - "Without natural affection" —
the Greek word (astorgos) refers to the breakdown of natural family bonds - "Having a form of
godliness, but denying the power thereof" — religious appearance without genuine transformation
Jesus connected lawlessness to spiritual coldness:
"And because iniquity shall abound, the love of many shall wax cold" (Matthew 24:12).
As sin increases, love decreases—both love for God and love for neighbor. The "many" whose love
grows cold suggests widespread apostasy within professing Christianity.
Jesus compared the last days to Noah and Lot:
"But as the days of Noe were, so shall also the coming of the Son of man be. For as in the days that
were before the flood they were eating and drinking, marrying and giving in marriage, until the day
that Noe entered into the ark, And knew not until the flood came, and took them all away; so shall also
the coming of the Son of man be" (Matthew 24:37-39).
"Likewise also as it was in the days of Lot; they did eat, they drank, they bought, they sold, they
planted, they builded; But the same day that Lot went out of Sodom it rained fire and brimstone from


---

heaven, and destroyed them all. Even thus shall it be in the day when the Son of man is revealed" (Luke
17:28-30).
What characterized these days? Genesis reveals:
In Noah's day: "And GOD saw that the wickedness of man was great in the earth, and that every
imagination of the thoughts of his heart was only evil continually... The earth also was corrupt before
God, and the earth was filled with violence" (Genesis 6:5, 11).
In Lot's day: "But the men of Sodom were wicked and sinners before the LORD exceedingly" (Genesis
13:13). The specific sin is detailed in Genesis 19:4-7.
Jude confirms: "Even as Sodom and Gomorrha, and the cities about them in like manner, giving
themselves over to fornication, and going after strange flesh, are set forth for an example, suffering the
vengeance of eternal fire" (Jude 1:7).
God's judgment includes giving people over to sin:
"Wherefore God also gave them up to uncleanness through the lusts of their own hearts, to dishonour
their own bodies between themselves: Who changed the truth of God into a lie, and worshipped and
served the creature more than the Creator... For this cause God gave them up unto vile affections: for
even their women did change the natural use into that which is against nature: And likewise also the
men, leaving the natural use of the woman, burned in their lust one toward another; men with men
working that which is unseemly, and receiving in themselves that recompence of their error which was
meet. And even as they did not like to retain God in their knowledge, God gave them over to a
reprobate mind" (Romans 1:24-28).
The progression Paul describes—from suppressing truth, to idolatry, to sexual immorality, to
homosexuality, to a debased mind—reflects the moral trajectory of modern culture.
The spirit of antichrist operates through deception:
"Now the Spirit speaketh expressly, that in the latter times some shall depart from the faith, giving heed
to seducing spirits, and doctrines of devils; Speaking lies in hypocrisy; having their conscience seared
with a hot iron" (1 Timothy 4:1-2).
"For the time will come when they will not endure sound doctrine; but after their own lusts shall they
heap to themselves teachers, having itching ears; And they shall turn away their ears from the truth,
and shall be turned unto fables" (2 Timothy 4:3-4).
5. The Spread of the Gospel
Current Conditions


---

Despite persecution and opposition, the gospel continues to spread globally. The church is growing
rapidly in Africa, Asia, and Latin America. Bible translation advances. Underground churches multiply
in hostile nations. Christianity has become a truly global faith.
What Scripture Declares
Jesus promised the gospel would reach all nations:
"And this gospel of the kingdom shall be preached in all the world for a witness unto all nations; and
then shall the end come" (Matthew 24:14).
The Greek word for "nations" (ethnos) refers to people groups—tribes, tongues, and peoples—not
merely political boundaries.
The Great Commission guarantees success:
"All power is given unto me in heaven and in earth. Go ye therefore, and teach all nations, baptizing
them in the name of the Father, and of the Son, and of the Holy Ghost: Teaching them to observe all
things whatsoever I have commanded you: and, lo, I am with you alway, even unto the end of the
world" (Matthew 28:18-20).
Christ commands the mission based on His universal authority and guarantees His presence until "the
end of the world" (literally, "the consummation of the age").
Revelation reveals the outcome:
"After this I beheld, and, lo, a great multitude, which no man could number, of all nations, and
kindreds, and people, and tongues, stood before the throne, and before the Lamb, clothed with white
robes, and palms in their hands" (Revelation 7:9).
This vision shows the completed harvest—representatives from every segment of humanity
worshipping the Lamb. The Great Commission will succeed.
The church cannot be overcome:
"And I say also unto thee, That thou art Peter, and upon this rock I will build my church; and the gates
of hell shall not prevail against it" (Matthew 16:18).
Gospel growth despite persecution fulfills Scripture:
"But I would ye should understand, brethren, that the things which happened unto me have fallen out
rather unto the furtherance of the gospel" (Philippians 1:12).
Paul's imprisonment advanced the gospel. This pattern continues—persecution scatters believers who
carry the gospel with them, as happened in Acts 8:1-4: "They that were scattered abroad went every
where preaching the word."


---

Isaiah prophesied: "So shall my word be that goeth forth out of my mouth: it shall not return unto me
void, but it shall accomplish that which I please, and it shall prosper in the thing whereto I sent it"
(Isaiah 55:11).
6. The Convergence of Signs
The Unique Convergence in Our Generation
Throughout the church age, individual signs have appeared. Persecution was severe under Rome. Wars
devastated medieval Europe. Moral decline characterized various periods. But never before have all the
major prophetic signs converged simultaneously:
- Israel restored to the land after nearly 2,000 years of diaspora - Jerusalem under Jewish sovereignty -
Global persecution of Christians at unprecedented scale - The gospel reaching all nations through
technology and missions - Moral conditions matching Jesus' comparison to Noah and Lot - Wars and
rumors of wars throughout the earth - Israel surrounded by hostile nations exactly as Zechariah
prophesied
What Scripture Declares
Jesus taught convergence as the key indicator:
"So likewise ye, when ye shall see all these things, know that it is near, even at the doors. Verily I say
unto you, This generation shall not pass, till all these things be fulfilled" (Matthew 24:33-34).
The phrase "all these things" indicates that the signs must appear together in the same generation.
The fig tree parable points to recognizable signs:
"Now learn a parable of the fig tree; When his branch is yet tender, and putteth forth leaves, ye know
that summer is nigh" (Matthew 24:32).
Just as a fig tree's budding indicates approaching summer, the convergence of prophetic signs indicates
Christ's approaching return.
Peter warned of scoffers in the last days:
"Knowing this first, that there shall come in the last days scoffers, walking after their own lusts, And
saying, Where is the promise of his coming? for since the fathers fell asleep, all things continue as they
were from the beginning of the creation" (2 Peter 3:3-4).
Skepticism about Christ's return is itself a sign of the times.
The principle of acceleration:


---

Jesus compared the signs to birth pangs (Matthew 24:8). Birth pains begin gradually but intensify in
both frequency and severity as delivery approaches. The convergence and intensification of signs
suggest we are in the final stages.
7. Living in Light of the End Times
What Scripture Commands
Watchfulness:
"Watch therefore: for ye know not what hour your Lord doth come" (Matthew 24:42).
"Therefore be ye also ready: for in such an hour as ye think not the Son of man cometh" (Matthew
24:44).
"Watch ye therefore, and pray always, that ye may be accounted worthy to escape all these things that
shall come to pass, and to stand before the Son of man" (Luke 21:36).
Sobriety and alertness:
"And that, knowing the time, that now it is high time to awake out of sleep: for now is our salvation
nearer than when we believed. The night is far spent, the day is at hand: let us therefore cast off the
works of darkness, and let us put on the armour of light" (Romans 13:11-12).
"But ye, brethren, are not in darkness, that that day should overtake you as a thief. Ye are all the
children of light, and the children of the day: we are not of the night, nor of darkness. Therefore let us
not sleep, as do others; but let us watch and be sober" (1 Thessalonians 5:4-6).
Readiness like the wise virgins:
"Then shall the kingdom of heaven be likened unto ten virgins, which took their lamps, and went forth
to meet the bridegroom. And five of them were wise, and five were foolish. They that were foolish took
their lamps, and took no oil with them: But the wise took oil in their vessels with their lamps. While the
bridegroom tarried, they all slumbered and slept. And at midnight there was a cry made, Behold, the
bridegroom cometh; go ye out to meet him... And they that were ready went in with him to the
marriage: and the door was shut" (Matthew 25:1-6, 10).
The oil represents the Holy Spirit and genuine faith. External religion without internal reality leaves
one unprepared.
Faithful service:
"Who then is a faithful and wise servant, whom his lord hath made ruler over his household, to give
them meat in due season? Blessed is that servant, whom his lord when he cometh shall find so doing"


---

(Matthew 24:45-46).
Endurance:
"But he that shall endure unto the end, the same shall be saved" (Matthew 24:13).
Proclamation:
"And this gospel of the kingdom shall be preached in all the world for a witness unto all nations; and
then shall the end come" (Matthew 24:14).
The urgency of the times demands faithful gospel witness.
Encouragement to one another:
"And let us consider one another to provoke unto love and to good works: Not forsaking the assembling
of ourselves together, as the manner of some is; but exhorting one another: and so much the more, as
ye see the day approaching" (Hebrews 10:24-25).
Purification:
"Beloved, now are we the sons of God, and it doth not yet appear what we shall be: but we know that,
when he shall appear, we shall be like him; for we shall see him as he is. And every man that hath this
hope in him purifieth himself, even as he is pure" (1 John 3:2-3).
Patient expectation:
"Be patient therefore, brethren, unto the coming of the Lord. Behold, the husbandman waiteth for the
precious fruit of the earth, and hath long patience for it, until he receive the early and latter rain. Be ye
also patient; stablish your hearts: for the coming of the Lord draweth nigh" (James 5:7-8).
8. Conclusion
Summary of Prophetic Alignment
Scripture reveals that the last days are characterized by:
1. Persecution of believers — "hated of all nations" (Matthew 24:9) 2. Wars and international
conflict — "nation against nation, kingdom against kingdom" (Luke 21:10) 3. Israel restored and
Jerusalem contested — "a burdensome stone for all people" (Zechariah 12:3) 4. Moral decline
matching Noah and Lot — "as the days of Noe were" (Matthew 24:37) 5. Global gospel
proclamation — "preached in all the world for a witness" (Matthew 24:14) 6. Convergence of all
signs — "when ye shall see all these things" (Matthew 24:33)
Each of these conditions exists in our generation with unprecedented clarity and intensity.


---

The Blessed Hope
"Looking for that blessed hope, and the glorious appearing of the great God and our Saviour Jesus
Christ" (Titus 2:13).
"For the Lord himself shall descend from heaven with a shout, with the voice of the archangel, and with
the trump of God: and the dead in Christ shall rise first: Then we which are alive and remain shall be
caught up together with them in the clouds, to meet the Lord in the air: and so shall we ever be with the
Lord. Wherefore comfort one another with these words" (1 Thessalonians 4:16-18).
The Final Call
"He which testifieth these things saith, Surely I come quickly. Amen. Even so, come, Lord Jesus"
(Revelation 22:20).
The prophetic signs are not given to produce fear but faith—not anxiety but anticipation. As Jesus
commanded: "And when these things begin to come to pass, then look up, and lift up your heads; for
your redemption draweth nigh" (Luke 21:28).
The appropriate response is threefold:
1. Faith — Trust in Christ alone for salvation: "Believe on the Lord Jesus Christ, and thou shalt be
saved" (Acts 16:31).
2. Faithfulness — Continue in obedience until He comes: "Be thou faithful unto death, and I will give
thee a crown of life" (Revelation 2:10).
3. Witness — Proclaim the gospel with urgency: "The fruit of the righteous is a tree of life; and he that
winneth souls is wise" (Proverbs 11:30).
"He that hath an ear, let him hear what the Spirit saith unto the churches" (Revelation 2:7).
Maranatha — Our Lord, come!


---

Part VI: Current Events
Chapter 12: Characteristics Analysis: The Fig Tree
Generation
Biblical Characteristics of End-Times Events
A Scripture-Interprets-Scripture Analysis
Purpose of This Document
This document does not name modern entities. It presents only what Scripture provides: descriptive
characteristics.
God's prophetic methodology is characteristics-based by design, not by accident or limitation. Scripture
identifies end-time powers and events through accumulated markers rather than direct names for
reasons rooted in the nature of prophecy itself:
Amos 3:7 — "Surely the Lord GOD will do nothing, but he revealeth his secret unto his servants the
prophets."
God does not hide truth from His people. He reveals it — but He reveals it in a way that requires
spiritual discernment and scriptural study. The characteristics He provides are sufficient for
identification by those who search the Scriptures.
2 Peter 1:20-21 — "Knowing this first, that no prophecy of the scripture is of any private
interpretation. For the prophecy came not in old time by the will of man: but holy men of God spake as
they were moved by the Holy Ghost."
Prophecy is not of "private interpretation" — it is not secret knowledge accessible only to initiates. The
Bible interprets itself. When we gather the characteristics God has scattered "here a little, and there a
little" (Isaiah 28:10), the cumulative testimony identifies what God intends His people to recognize.


---

The reader is responsible for matching these biblically-given markers to observable, verifiable
reality. This is itself biblical — God identifies prophetic powers by their attributes, not their names, so
that each generation can discern the times through the Spirit's guidance and the testimony of Scripture.
Revelation 13:9 — "If any man have an ear, let him hear."
The call is universal. The characteristics are public. The identification is possible for all who will
search.
Foundational Principle: Identification by Characteristics, Not Names
Scripture employs a consistent methodology for identifying prophetic entities and events: descriptive
characteristics rather than direct naming. This approach serves multiple purposes:
1. Prevents premature exposure of entities that would otherwise suppress or alter the prophecy 2.
Ensures timeless applicability across generations who must discern the times 3. Requires spiritual
discernment — those with "ears to hear" recognize the markers (Revelation 13:9) 4. Allows
progressive revelation as characteristics accumulate and clarify over time
The principle is established in Isaiah 28:10: "For precept must be upon precept, precept upon precept;
line upon line, line upon line; here a little, and there a little." God reveals truth through accumulated,
cross-referenced details scattered throughout Scripture.
Part I: The Foundation — Genesis to the Prophets
A. The Protoevangelium: Genesis 3:15
The entire prophetic framework begins here:
Genesis 3:15 — "And I will put enmity between thee and the woman, and between thy seed and her
seed; it shall bruise thy head, and thou shalt bruise his heel."
Foundational Characteristics: - Enmity — Perpetual conflict between two seeds - The serpent's
seed — Those aligned with Satan's rebellion - The woman's seed — Those aligned with God,
culminating in Christ - Bruising the heel — Temporary harm to the woman's seed (the cross) -
Bruising the head — Fatal destruction of the serpent (the final victory)
This establishes the cosmic conflict that runs through all Scripture and reaches its climax in Revelation
12, where the same serpent, the dragon, makes war with "the remnant of her seed."
B. Jacob's "Last Days" Prophecy: Genesis 49


---

Genesis 49:1 — "And Jacob called unto his sons, and said, Gather yourselves together, that I may tell
you that which shall befall you in the last days."
This is the first explicit use of "last days" in Scripture. Jacob's prophecy concerning Judah contains a
Messianic marker:
Genesis 49:10 — "The sceptre shall not depart from Judah, nor a lawgiver from between his feet, until
Shiloh come; and unto him shall the gathering of the people be."
Characteristics: - The scepter (governmental authority) remains with Judah until Shiloh (the Messiah)
- When Shiloh comes, the gathering of the peoples occurs
C. Balaam's "Latter Days" Prophecy: Numbers 24
Numbers 24:14 — "Come therefore, and I will advertise thee what this people shall do to thy people in
the latter days."
Numbers 24:17 — "I shall see him, but not now: I shall behold him, but not nigh: there shall come a
Star out of Jacob, and a Sceptre shall rise out of Israel"
Characteristics of the Coming One: - A Star out of Jacob - A Sceptre rising out of Israel - Not
appearing in Balaam's time ("not now," "not nigh") - Ultimate victory over enemies
Part II: Characteristics of End-Time Global Conditions
A. The Moral Climate of the Last Days
2 Timothy 3:1-5 provides the most comprehensive catalogue of social conditions marking "perilous
times":
Characteristic | Greek Root Meaning | Observable Manifestation
Lovers of their own selves | φIλαυτοι (philautoi) | Narcissism, self-absorption Covetous |
φιλIργυροι (philarguroi) | Love of money as supreme value Boasters | IλαζIνες (alazones) | Empty
bragging, self-promotion Proud | IπερIφανοι (huperIphanoi) | Appearing above others, arrogance
Blasphemers | βλIσφηµοι (blasphImoi) | Speaking against God openly Disobedient to parents |
γονεIσιν IπειθεIς | Breakdown of family authority Unthankful | IχIριστοι (acharistoi) |
Entitlement mentality Unholy | IνIσιοι (anosioi) | No reverence for sacred things Without natural
affection | Iστοργοι (astorgoi) | Loss of instinctive family bonds Trucebreakers | Iσπονδοι
(aspondoi) | Breaking covenants, no reconciliation False accusers | διIβολοι (diaboloi) | Slanderers
(literally "devils") Incontinent | IκρατεIς (akrateis) | No self-control Fierce | IνIµεροι (anImeroi) |
Savage, uncivilized brutality Despisers of those that are good | IφιλIγαθοι | Active hatred of
goodness Traitors | προδIται (prodotai) | Betrayers, turncoats Heady | προπετεIς (propeteis) |


---

Reckless, rash Highminded | τετυφωµIνοι (tetyphImenoi) | Puffed up, conceited Lovers of pleasures
more than lovers of God | Hedonism as religion
The climactic marker: "Having a form of godliness, but denying the power thereof" — religious
appearance without transformative reality. This describes institutional religion divorced from genuine
spiritual power.
B. Economic Characteristics of the Last Days
James 5:1-8 provides critical economic markers often overlooked:
James 5:1-3 — "Go to now, ye rich men, weep and howl for your miseries that shall come upon you.
Your riches are corrupted, and your garments are motheaten. Your gold and silver is cankered; and the
rust of them shall be a witness against you, and shall eat your flesh as it were fire. Ye have heaped
treasure together for the last days."
Characteristics: - Unprecedented accumulation of wealth ("heaped treasure together for the last days")
- Corruption of riches — wealth itself becomes witness against its holders - This is explicitly placed in
the last days
James 5:4 — "Behold, the hire of the labourers who have reaped down your fields, which is of you kept
back by fraud, crieth: and the cries of them which have reaped are entered into the ears of the Lord of
sabaoth."
Characteristics: - Wage theft ("kept back by fraud") - The cry of defrauded workers reaches God -
Systemic labor exploitation
James 5:5-6 — "Ye have lived in pleasure on the earth, and been wanton; ye have nourished your
hearts, as in a day of slaughter. Ye have condemned and killed the just; and he doth not resist you."
Characteristics: - Hedonistic luxury among the wealthy - Condemnation and killing of the righteous -
The righteous do not resist — peaceful endurance
James 5:7-8 — "Be patient therefore, brethren, unto the coming of the Lord... for the coming of the
Lord draweth nigh."
These economic conditions directly precede the Lord's coming.
C. Intellectual Climate of the Last Days
2 Timothy 3:7 — "Ever learning, and never able to come to the knowledge of the truth"
This describes a paradox: unprecedented access to information alongside an inability to synthesize it
into truth. Information abundance without wisdom.


---

2 Timothy 4:3-4 — "For the time will come when they will not endure sound doctrine; but after their
own lusts shall they heap to themselves teachers, having itching ears; And they shall turn away their
ears from the truth, and shall be turned unto fables."
Characteristics: - Rejection of absolute truth claims ("sound doctrine") - Self-selection of teachers who
affirm existing beliefs - Preference for comfortable narratives over challenging truth - Exchange of
revelation for mythology ("fables")
D. Spiritual Climate: Apostasy
2 Thessalonians 2:3 — "Let no man deceive you by any means: for that day shall not come, except
there come a falling away first"
The Greek IποστασIα (apostasia) indicates: - Not mere unbelief, but departure from previously
held truth - Institutional, not merely individual - Precondition for the revelation of the "man of sin"
1 Timothy 4:1-3 — "Now the Spirit speaketh expressly, that in the latter times some shall depart from
the faith, giving heed to seducing spirits, and doctrines of devils; Speaking lies in hypocrisy; having
their conscience seared with a hot iron; Forbidding to marry, and commanding to abstain from meats."
Specific doctrinal markers: - Mandatory celibacy imposed on religious leaders - Dietary prohibitions
elevated to salvific importance - Human traditions superseding biblical commands
E. Scoffers and Willful Ignorance
2 Peter 3:3-4 — "Knowing this first, that there shall come in the last days scoffers, walking after their
own lusts, And saying, Where is the promise of his coming? for since the fathers fell asleep, all things
continue as they were from the beginning of the creation."
This describes uniformitarian thinking applied to eschatology — the assumption that because
conditions have remained stable, they will continue indefinitely. The text explicitly connects this to: -
Walking after personal desires (motive) - Willful ignorance of prior divine interventions (2 Peter 3:5-6)
F. Mockers in the Last Time
Jude 17-19 — "But, beloved, remember ye the words which were spoken before of the apostles of our
Lord Jesus Christ; How that they told you there should be mockers in the last time, who should walk
after their own ungodly lusts. These be they who separate themselves, sensual, having not the Spirit."
Characteristics of mockers: - Walking after ungodly lusts - Causing division ("separate themselves") -
Sensual (governed by natural instincts rather than Spirit) - Devoid of the Spirit
Part III: Characteristics of End-Time Players


---

A. The First Beast of Revelation 13 (Verses 1-10)
Scripture never directly names this entity but provides extensive identifying characteristics:
Origin Characteristics: - "Rise up out of the sea" (v.1) — Sea = "peoples, and multitudes, and nations,
and tongues" (Revelation 17:15). Arises from populated, established civilizations - "Seven heads and
ten horns" — Direct link to Daniel 7's fourth beast (Rome) and its fragmentation
Composite Nature: - "Like unto a leopard" — Greece (Daniel 7:6) - "Feet of a bear" — Medo-Persia
(Daniel 7:5) - "Mouth of a lion" — Babylon (Daniel 7:4)
This indicates an entity that absorbs and perpetuates elements of all preceding world empires — a
successor power to pagan Rome that carries forward Babylonian, Persian, and Greek characteristics.
Behavioral Characteristics: Verse | Characteristic | Interpretive Significance
v.2 | "The dragon gave him his power, and his seat, and great authority" | Direct satanic empowerment;
occupies the dragon's former "seat" (throne city) v.3 | "One of his heads as it were wounded to death;
and his deadly wound was healed" | Historical near-extinction followed by recovery v.3 | "All the world
wondered after the beast" | Global admiration and following v.4 | "They worshipped the dragon which
gave power unto the beast" | Worship of Satan through worship of this power v.5 | "A mouth speaking
great things and blasphemies" | Claims and titles that belong only to God v.5 | "Power was given unto
him to continue forty and two months" | 42 months = 1,260 days = time, times, and half a time = 1,260
years (day-year principle) v.6 | "Blaspheme his name, and his tabernacle, and them that dwell in
heaven" | Claims priestly/mediatorial functions; attacks heavenly sanctuary ministry v.7 | "Make war
with the saints, and to overcome them" | Persecuting power with authority over believers v.7 | "Power
over all kindreds, and tongues, and nations" | Universal jurisdictional claims v.8 | "All that dwell upon
the earth shall worship him" | Universal religious obeisance
The Deadly Wound and Its Healing (v.3): This is a defining characteristic — a historical period of
apparent destruction followed by remarkable recovery. The wound comes by "a sword" (v.14),
indicating governmental/military action against this power.
Revelation 13:10 — The Lex Talionis: "He that leadeth into captivity shall go into captivity: he that
killeth with the sword must be killed with the sword. Here is the patience and the faith of the saints."
Characteristics: - The first beast leads others into captivity — and itself goes into captivity - It kills
with the sword — and is wounded by the sword - This is the "patience and faith of the saints" — they
wait for God's justice
B. The Daniel 7 Little Horn — Complete Characteristics
Daniel 7 provides additional characteristics of the same power:
Reference | Characteristic | Significance


---

Dan 7:8 | "Eyes like the eyes of man" | Human intelligence directing it Dan 7:8 | "A mouth speaking
great things" | Blasphemous claims Dan 7:8, 20, 24 | "Before whom three fell... three of the first horns
plucked up by the roots" | Uproots/subdues three of the ten kingdoms Dan 7:20 | "Look was more stout
than his fellows" | Prominence among the ten; appears greater Dan 7:21 | "Made war with the saints,
and prevailed against them" | Persecuting power Dan 7:25 | "Think to change times and laws" |
Attempts to alter God's times (Sabbath) and law (the Ten Commandments) Dan 7:25 | "Wear out
the saints of the Most High" | Persecution through attrition; long-duration pressure Dan 7:25 | "Time
and times and the dividing of time" | 3½ prophetic years = 1,260 day-years Dan 7:25 | "Given into his
hand" | Saints temporarily under his authority
The critical characteristic: "Think to change times and laws" — This power presumes to modify
what God has established, particularly His law and His appointed times.
C. The Second Beast of Revelation 13 (Verses 11-18)
Origin Characteristics: - "Coming up out of the earth" (v.11) — Contrast to the first beast's "sea"
origin. Arises from a sparsely populated region, a "wilderness" area - Timing: Appears as the first beast
receives its wound and "goes into captivity" (v.10)
Appearance vs. Reality: - "Two horns like a lamb" (v.11) — Lamb-like appearance: Christ-like,
gentle, peaceful - Two horns WITHOUT crowns — Unlike the first beast's crowned horns;
non-monarchical; republican - "Spake as a dragon" (v.11) — Dragon speech: satanic
legislative/decreeing power
Key Principle: "Speak" = Legislate
The Hebrew conception of "speaking" in relation to powers involves authoritative decree. Daniel 3 and
Daniel 6 demonstrate this:
- Daniel 3: Nebuchadnezzar "made a decree" (spoke) requiring worship of the image on pain of death -
Daniel 6: Darius "signed the writing and the decree" (spoke) prohibiting prayer to any god except
himself
When the second beast "spake as a dragon," it indicates this lamb-like power will eventually legislate
persecution — using law to compel worship and punish dissenters.
Functional Characteristics: Verse | Action | Interpretive Significance
v.12 | "Exerciseth all the power of the first beast before him" | Uses identical coercive methods v.12 |
"Causeth the earth and them which dwell therein to worship the first beast" | Promotes/enforces the first
beast's religious claims v.13 | "Doeth great wonders, so that he maketh fire come down from heaven" |
Miraculous displays; counterfeit divine approval v.14 | "Deceiveth them that dwell on the earth by the
means of those miracles" | Deception is primary mode of operation v.14 | "Saying to them that dwell on
the earth, that they should make an image to the beast" | Initiates image-making; democratic process
("them that dwell") v.15 | "He had power to give life unto the image of the beast" | Animates/empowers


---

the image to function v.15 | "That the image of the beast should both speak" | The image itself legislates
— creates laws v.15 | "Cause that as many as would not worship the image of the beast should be
killed" | Death penalty for non-compliance v.16-17 | "Causeth all... to receive a mark... that no man
might buy or sell" | Economic enforcement through commercial exclusion
Connection to Revelation 12:16: "And the earth helped the woman, and the earth opened her mouth,
and swallowed up the flood which the dragon cast out of his mouth."
The "earth" that helped the woman (the church fleeing persecution) is the same "earth" from which the
second beast arises. Initially protective, this power eventually transforms.
D. The Number of the Beast: 666
Revelation 13:18 — "Here is wisdom. Let him that hath understanding count the number of the beast:
for it is the number of a man; and his number is Six hundred threescore and six."
Characteristics: - "Here is wisdom" — Requires discernment to understand - "Let him that hath
understanding count" — Calculation is involved - "The number of a man" — Connected to a specific
human title or name - "Six hundred threescore and six" — 666
The invitation to "count" indicates this is solvable by those who seek wisdom.
E. The Image of the Beast
The "image" is not merely a statue but a functional replica — something that reproduces the essential
characteristics of the first beast:
1. Church-state union (the first beast's defining feature: religious power wielding civil authority) 2.
Compulsory worship backed by governmental enforcement 3. The image "speaks" — it legislates,
creates binding decrees
Daniel 3 provides the typology: Nebuchadnezzar's image required universal worship on penalty of
death. The end-time image reproduces this pattern.
F. The Dragon
Revelation 12:9 — "And the great dragon was cast out, that old serpent, called the Devil, and Satan,
which deceiveth the whole world"
Revelation directly names this power: Satan himself. But in prophetic symbology, the dragon also
represents:
- Pagan Rome (Matthew 2 — Herod's attempt to kill the Christ child while Rome ruled) - Any
governmental system directly wielded as Satan's instrument - The ultimate power behind all earthly


---

persecuting entities
The Dragon's Defining Characteristic: "Deceiveth the whole world" (12:9)
G. The Man of Sin / Son of Perdition
2 Thessalonians 2:3-4 provides characteristics without naming:
Characteristic | Scriptural Description | Interpretive Significance
Title | "Man of sin" | Sin personified in a system/office Title | "Son of perdition" | Same title as Judas
(John 17:12); betrayer from within Action | "Opposeth and exalteth himself above all that is called
God" | Claims supremacy over all religions Action | "Sitteth in the temple of God" | Occupies God's
place in His church Claim | "Shewing himself that he is God" | Divine prerogatives claimed Timing |
"Revealed in his time" after restrainer removed (v.6-7) | Cannot fully manifest until a hindering power
is removed Method | "After the working of Satan with all power and signs and lying wonders" (v.9) |
Satanically empowered miraculous displays Effect | "All deceivableness of unrighteousness" (v.10) |
Comprehensive deception
The "mystery of iniquity" was already working in Paul's day (v.7), indicating this is not a single
individual but a system that develops over time.
H. The Antichrist — 1 John's Characteristics
1 John 2:18 — "Little children, it is the last time: and as ye have heard that antichrist shall come, even
now are there many antichrists; whereby we know that it is the last time."
Characteristics: - "It is the last time" — The presence of antichrist(s) indicates the last time - "Even
now are there many antichrists" — Multiple manifestations, not a single individual - "They went out
from us, but they were not of us" (v.19) — Apostasy from within the church
1 John 2:22 — "Who is a liar but he that denieth that Jesus is the Christ? He is antichrist, that denieth
the Father and the Son."
Characteristics: - Denies Jesus is the Christ - Denies the Father and the Son - A "liar" — deception is
fundamental
1 John 4:2-3 — "Hereby know ye the Spirit of God: Every spirit that confesseth that Jesus Christ is
come in the flesh is of God: And every spirit that confesseth not that Jesus Christ is come in the flesh is
not of God: and this is that spirit of antichrist, whereof ye have heard that it should come; and even
now already is it in the world."
Characteristics: - Does not confess Jesus Christ is come in the flesh - The spirit of antichrist was
"already in the world" in John's day - It is a spirit — a system of thought, not merely a person


---

2 John 7 — "For many deceivers are entered into the world, who confess not that Jesus Christ is come
in the flesh. This is a deceiver and an antichrist."
Characteristics: - "Many deceivers" — numerous, not singular - Denial of the incarnation
I. Babylon the Great
Revelation 17-18 characterizes without naming directly:
Religious Identity: - "MYSTERY, BABYLON THE GREAT, THE MOTHER OF HARLOTS AND
ABOMINATIONS OF THE EARTH" (17:5) - "Mother" indicates originating system from which others
derive - "Harlots" (plural) — daughter systems sharing her characteristics - "Mystery" — claim to
esoteric religious knowledge
Political Relationships: - "Sitteth upon many waters" (17:1) — Rules over "peoples, and multitudes,
and nations, and tongues" (17:15) - "Kings of the earth have committed fornication" (17:2) — Illicit
church-state unions - "Reigneth over the kings of the earth" (17:18) — Political supremacy
Economic Characteristics (Revelation 18): - Merchants enriched through her (18:3) - "The
merchandise of gold, and silver, and precious stones... and slaves, and souls of men" (18:12-13) -
Global commercial system intertwined with her existence
Identifying Markers: - "The woman was arrayed in purple and scarlet colour" (17:4) — Official
vestments - "Decked with gold and precious stones and pearls" (17:4) — Immense wealth display -
"Seven heads are seven mountains, on which the woman sitteth" (17:9) — Geographic location -
"Drunken with the blood of the saints, and with the blood of the martyrs of Jesus" (17:6) — Persecuting
history
The Three-Part Babylon (Revelation 16:13, 19):
Revelation 16:13 reveals the final coalition: "Three unclean spirits like frogs come out of the mouth of
the dragon, and out of the mouth of the beast, and out of the mouth of the false prophet."
Then 16:19: "The great city was divided into three parts."
This indicates Babylon in its final form is a tripartite alliance: 1. The Dragon —
Spiritualism/paganism/occult power 2. The Beast — Papal Rome and allied apostate Christianity 3.
The False Prophet — Apostate Protestantism (the second beast having fully transformed)
J. Gog and Magog — Ezekiel 38-39
Ezekiel 38:8 — "After many days thou shalt be visited: in the latter years thou shalt come into the land
that is brought back from the sword, and is gathered out of many people, against the mountains of
Israel"


---

Ezekiel 38:16 — "And thou shalt come up against my people of Israel, as a cloud to cover the land; it
shall be in the latter days"
Characteristics of Gog and the Coalition: - Occurs in "the latter years" and "the latter days" - Comes
from "the north parts" (Ezek 38:15; 39:2) - Coalition includes: Persia, Ethiopia, Libya, Gomer,
Togarmah (Ezek 38:5-6) - Attacks Israel "as a cloud to cover the land" - Attacks "the land that is
brought back from the sword" — restored Israel - Attacks those "gathered out of many people" - God
fights against them directly (Ezek 38:18-22) - Destruction includes pestilence, blood, rain, hailstones,
fire, brimstone (Ezek 38:22)
Revelation 20:8 connects Gog and Magog to the post-millennial final deception.
Part IV: Characteristics of End-Time Events
A. The Abomination of Desolation
Matthew 24:15 — "When ye therefore shall see the abomination of desolation, spoken of by Daniel the
prophet, stand in the holy place, (whoso readeth, let him understand:)"
Christ's parenthetical — "whoso readeth, let him understand" — signals that this requires careful study
of Daniel to identify.
Daniel 9:27 — "For the overspreading of abominations he shall make it desolate" Daniel 11:31 —
"They shall place the abomination that maketh desolate" Daniel 12:11 — "From the time that... the
abomination that maketh desolate set up"
Characteristics: - Something "placed" or "set up" — an institution or system, not a single event -
Connected to the cessation of the "daily" (true worship/mediation) - Results in "desolation" — spiritual
emptiness where truth once stood - Involves taking away and substituting — counterfeit for genuine
B. The Mark of the Beast
Revelation 13:16-17 — "And he causeth all, both small and great, rich and poor, free and bond, to
receive a mark in their right hand, or in their foreheads: And that no man might buy or sell, save he
that had the mark, or the name of the beast, or the number of his name."
Characteristics of the Mark: - Universal application ("all") - Cross-class enforcement (social status
irrelevant) - Located in "forehead" (intellectual assent/belief) OR "right hand" (actions/works) -
Economic enforcement mechanism ("buy or sell") - Alternative to the "seal of God" in foreheads
(Revelation 7:3)
Contrast with the Seal of God: - The seal is in the forehead only — requires genuine
intellectual/spiritual commitment - The mark can be in forehead OR hand — compliance without


---

conviction suffices - This reflects forced vs. willing worship
Connection to Sabbath/Worship: The mark involves worship — "worship the beast and his image"
(14:9). It is the sign of allegiance to the beast's authority, contrasted with the seal of God which
signifies allegiance to the Creator.
Exodus 31:13, 17 identifies the Sabbath as God's "sign" between Him and His people — a mark of
creative and redemptive authority.
Ezekiel 20:12, 20 — "Moreover also I gave them my sabbaths, to be a sign between me and them, that
they might know that I am the LORD that sanctify them... And hallow my sabbaths; and they shall be a
sign between me and you, that ye may know that I am the LORD your God."
The Sabbath is explicitly called a sign. The mark of the beast is the counterfeit sign of an alternate
authority.
C. The Great Tribulation
Matthew 24:21 — "For then shall be great tribulation, such as was not since the beginning of the
world to this time, no, nor ever shall be."
Characteristics: - Unprecedented severity - Universal scope - Shortened for the elect's sake (v.22)
Daniel 12:1 — "There shall be a time of trouble, such as never was since there was a nation even to
that same time: and at that time thy people shall be delivered"
The time of trouble is immediately preceding deliverance — the final crisis before Christ's return.
D. Signs in Nature and Society
Luke 21:25-26 catalogues observable signs: - Signs in sun, moon, and stars - Distress of nations with
perplexity - Sea and waves roaring - Men's hearts failing them for fear - Powers of heaven shaken
Matthew 24:7-8 — "Nation shall rise against nation, and kingdom against kingdom: and there shall
be famines, and pestilences, and earthquakes, in divers places. All these are the beginning of sorrows."
The phrase "beginning of sorrows" (IδIνων — birth pangs) indicates increasing frequency and
intensity — like labor contractions.
E. The Latter Rain and Cosmic Signs: Joel 2
Joel 2:28-32 — "And it shall come to pass afterward, that I will pour out my spirit upon all flesh; and
your sons and your daughters shall prophesy, your old men shall dream dreams, your young men shall
see visions: And also upon the servants and upon the handmaids in those days will I pour out my spirit.
And I will shew wonders in the heavens and in the earth, blood, and fire, and pillars of smoke. The sun


---

shall be turned into darkness, and the moon into blood, before the great and the terrible day of the
LORD come. And it shall come to pass, that whosoever shall call on the name of the LORD shall be
delivered"
Characteristics: - Outpouring of the Spirit on "all flesh" - Prophesying by sons and daughters -
Dreams by old men - Visions by young men - Spirit poured out even on servants and handmaids -
Wonders in heavens and earth: blood, fire, pillars of smoke - Sun turned to darkness - Moon turned to
blood - All this "before the great and terrible day of the LORD" - Deliverance for those who call on
the name of the LORD
F. The Day of the LORD — Zechariah 14
Zechariah 14:1-4 — "Behold, the day of the LORD cometh... For I will gather all nations against
Jerusalem to battle... Then shall the LORD go forth, and fight against those nations, as when he fought
in the day of battle. And his feet shall stand in that day upon the mount of Olives, which is before
Jerusalem on the east, and the mount of Olives shall cleave in the midst thereof toward the east and
toward the west, and there shall be a very great valley"
Characteristics: - All nations gathered against Jerusalem - The LORD goes forth to fight - His feet
stand on the mount of Olives - The mount of Olives cleaves in two - Creates a great valley
Zechariah 14:9 — "And the LORD shall be king over all the earth: in that day shall there be one
LORD, and his name one."
G. The Gospel Proclamation
Matthew 24:14 — "And this gospel of the kingdom shall be preached in all the world for a witness
unto all nations; and then shall the end come."
The end does not come until: - The gospel reaches every nation - It serves as a "witness" — testimony
requiring response - This is fulfilled, then the end comes
Revelation 14:6-12 — The Three Angels' Messages represent the final gospel proclamation:
First Angel: "Fear God, and give glory to him; for the hour of his judgment is come: and worship him
that made heaven, and earth, and the sea, and the fountains of waters." - Call to worship the Creator
(Sabbath connection via creation language) - Announcement that judgment has arrived
Second Angel: "Babylon is fallen, is fallen, that great city, because she made all nations drink of the
wine of the wrath of her fornication." - Proclamation of Babylon's fall - Call to recognize her corruption
Third Angel: Warning against receiving the mark of the beast - Most solemn warning in Scripture -
Wrath of God without mixture promised


---

Part V: The "Speaking" of Powers — How Scripture Defines
Governmental Action
A. The Biblical Definition of Power "Speaking"
When Revelation 13:11 describes the second beast as "speaking as a dragon," it employs a Hebrew
concept foreign to modern Western thinking. In Scripture, when a power "speaks," it legislates and
decrees.
Daniel 3 Paradigm: - Nebuchadnezzar "made an image of gold" (v.1) - An herald "cried aloud"
(spoke) the decree (v.4) - "To you it is commanded, O people, nations, and languages" (v.4) - Universal
worship required: "Fall down and worship the golden image" (v.5) - Death penalty for non-compliance:
"Shall be cast into the midst of a burning fiery furnace" (v.6)
Daniel 6 Paradigm: - A "decree" was proposed (v.7) - The king "signed the writing and the decree"
(v.9) - "Whosoever shall ask a petition of any God or man for thirty days, save of thee, O king, he shall
be cast into the den of lions" (v.7) - Prayer itself criminalized
Key Elements in Both: 1. Legislative action ("decree," "command") 2. Universal application ("all
people, nations, and languages") 3. Religious requirement (worship the image / pray only to the king) 4.
Death penalty for disobedience (furnace / lions)
B. Application to Revelation 13
When the second beast "spake as a dragon," it means this lamb-like power will eventually: 1. Legislate
religious requirements 2. Apply them universally 3. Enforce them with penalties (including death and
economic exclusion)
The progression is clear: - "Two horns like a lamb" — appears Christ-like (religious liberty, separation
of church and state) - "Spake as a dragon" — eventually legislates like pagan Rome or papal Rome
The "image to the beast" (v.14) is precisely this: the reproduction of church-state union in the second
beast's territory.
Part VI: The Remnant — Counter-Characteristics
A. Identification of the Remnant
Revelation 12:17 — "And the dragon was wroth with the woman, and went to make war with the
remnant of her seed, which keep the commandments of God, and have the testimony of Jesus Christ."


---

Two Defining Characteristics: 1. Keep the commandments of God — All ten, including the fourth
2. Have the testimony of Jesus Christ — The spirit of prophecy (Revelation 19:10)
Revelation 14:12 — "Here is the patience of the saints: here are they that keep the commandments of
God, and the faith of Jesus."
Again, two markers: 1. Commandment-keeping 2. The faith OF Jesus (not merely faith IN Jesus — His
actual quality of faith)
B. The Sealed Company
Revelation 7:2-4 — "Seal of the living God... sealed the servants of our God in their foreheads... an
hundred and forty and four thousand"
Revelation 14:1-5 characterizes the 144,000: - "Father's name written in their foreheads" — Contrast to
mark of beast - "Not defiled with women" — Not participating in false religious systems ("virgins") -
"Follow the Lamb whithersoever he goeth" — Complete obedience - "In their mouth was found no
guile" — Perfect honesty - "Without fault before the throne of God" — Character perfection through
Christ
C. The Faithful Through the Tribulation
Revelation 15:2 — "Them that had gotten the victory over the beast, and over his image, and over his
mark, and over the number of his name"
The overcomers are identified by what they refused: - Did not worship the beast - Did not worship his
image - Did not receive his mark - Did not accept his number/name
Revelation 20:4 — "I saw the souls of them that were beheaded for the witness of Jesus, and for the
word of God, and which had not worshipped the beast, neither his image, neither had received his mark
upon their foreheads, or in their hands"
D. The Laodicean Condition — End-Time Church
Revelation 3:14-22 describes the final church age:
Revelation 3:15-17 — "I know thy works, that thou art neither cold nor hot: I would thou wert cold or
hot. So then because thou art lukewarm, and neither cold nor hot, I will spue thee out of my mouth.
Because thou sayest, I am rich, and increased with goods, and have need of nothing; and knowest not
that thou art wretched, and miserable, and poor, and blind, and naked."
Characteristics: - Lukewarm — neither cold nor hot - Self-deception about spiritual condition -
Claims to be rich and self-sufficient - Actually wretched, miserable, poor, blind, and naked - Does not
know its true condition


---

Revelation 3:20 — "Behold, I stand at the door, and knock"
Christ is depicted outside the Laodicean church, seeking entry.
Part VII: The Return of Christ — Characteristics of the Event
A. Visibility
Matthew 24:27 — "For as the lightning cometh out of the east, and shineth even unto the west; so
shall also the coming of the Son of man be."
- Universal visibility - No secret rapture — as public as lightning across the sky
Revelation 1:7 — "Behold, he cometh with clouds; and every eye shall see him"
B. Audibility
1 Thessalonians 4:16 — "The Lord himself shall descend from heaven with a shout, with the voice of
the archangel, and with the trump of God"
Three sounds: 1. A shout 2. The archangel's voice 3. The trumpet of God
Matthew 24:31 — "He shall send his angels with a great sound of a trumpet"
C. Accompaniment
Matthew 25:31 — "When the Son of man shall come in his glory, and all the holy angels with him"
- Personal return ("the Lord himself") - Angelic host accompaniment - Great glory
Jude 14-15 — "And Enoch also, the seventh from Adam, prophesied of these, saying, Behold, the Lord
cometh with ten thousands of his saints, To execute judgment upon all"
This is the oldest recorded prophecy of the Second Coming, from Enoch himself: - The Lord comes -
With ten thousands of His saints (holy ones) - To execute judgment upon all - To convict all the
ungodly
D. Physical Effects
Revelation 6:14-17 — Mountains and islands moved, the heavens departed as a scroll, universal terror
among the wicked.


---

2 Peter 3:10 — "The heavens shall pass away with a great noise, and the elements shall melt with
fervent heat, the earth also and the works that are therein shall be burned up."
E. Resurrection and Translation
1 Thessalonians 4:16-17 — "The dead in Christ shall rise first: Then we which are alive and remain
shall be caught up together with them in the clouds, to meet the Lord in the air"
Order of events: 1. Christ descends 2. Dead in Christ rise 3. Living believers translated 4. Together
caught up to meet Christ in the air
Part VIII: The Final Old Testament Prophecy — Malachi 4
Malachi 4:1-2 — "For, behold, the day cometh, that shall burn as an oven; and all the proud, yea, and
all that do wickedly, shall be stubble: and the day that cometh shall burn them up, saith the LORD of
hosts, that it shall leave them neither root nor branch. But unto you that fear my name shall the Sun of
righteousness arise with healing in his wings"
Characteristics: - The day burns as an oven - The proud and wicked become stubble - They are burned
up — "neither root nor branch" - But to those who fear God's name: the Sun of righteousness arises -
Healing in His wings
Malachi 4:5-6 — "Behold, I will send you Elijah the prophet before the coming of the great and
dreadful day of the LORD: And he shall turn the heart of the fathers to the children, and the heart of
the children to their fathers, lest I come and smite the earth with a curse."
Characteristics: - Elijah is sent before the great and dreadful day - His work: turning hearts — fathers
to children, children to fathers - This prevents the earth being smitten with a curse - The Old Testament
closes with this warning
Part IX: Time-Related Markers
A. The "Time of the End"
Daniel 12:4 — "But thou, O Daniel, shut up the words, and seal the book, even to the time of the end:
many shall run to and fro, and knowledge shall be increased."
Characteristics of the "time of the end": - Unsealing of Daniel's prophecies — previously sealed
portions become understandable - Greatly increased travel ("run to and fro") - Explosion of knowledge
Daniel 12:9-10 — "The words are closed up and sealed till the time of the end. Many shall be purified,
and made white, and tried; but the wicked shall do wickedly: and none of the wicked shall understand;


---

but the wise shall understand."
At the time of the end: - The wise will understand what had been sealed - The wicked will not
understand - Purification and trial intensify
B. The Hosea 6:2 Pattern
Hosea 6:2 — "After two days will he revive us: in the third day he will raise us up, and we shall live in
his sight."
Combined with 2 Peter 3:8 — "One day is with the Lord as a thousand years, and a thousand years as
one day."
And Psalm 90:4 — "For a thousand years in thy sight are but as yesterday when it is past."
This creates a prophetic framework: - Two "days" (2,000 years) of apparent death/scattering - Revival
"in the third day" (beginning of the third millennium from Christ)
C. The Generational Limit
Psalm 90:10 — "The days of our years are threescore years and ten; and if by reason of strength they
be fourscore years"
Applied to Israel's restoration (1948), this suggests: - 70 years = 2017 - 80 years = 2027
Matthew 24:32-34 — "Now learn a parable of the fig tree; When his branch is yet tender, and putteth
forth leaves, ye know that summer is nigh: So likewise ye, when ye shall see all these things, know that
it is near, even at the doors. Verily I say unto you, This generation shall not pass, till all these things be
fulfilled."
D. The 6,000-Year Framework
The creation week establishes a pattern: - Six days of labor - Seventh day rest (Sabbath)
Applied prophetically (day = 1,000 years): - 6,000 years of human history - 1,000-year Sabbath rest
(millennial reign — Revelation 20)
This is not "setting dates" but recognizing the biblical pattern of seven-day weeks applied to history.
Conclusion: The Purpose of Characteristics-Based Identification
Scripture's method of identifying end-time events and players through characteristics rather than direct
names serves the faithful across all ages. Each generation can examine current developments against


---

biblical markers and discern the times.
1 Thessalonians 5:4-6 — "But ye, brethren, are not in darkness, that that day should overtake you as a
thief. Ye are all the children of light, and the children of the day: we are not of the night, nor of
darkness. Therefore let us not sleep, as do others; but let us watch and be sober."
The faithful are not overtaken as by a thief — they recognize the season through the accumulated
testimony of Scripture's prophetic characteristics.
Luke 21:28 — "And when these things begin to come to pass, then look up, and lift up your heads; for
your redemption draweth nigh."

Part VII: Conclusion
Chapter 13: The Master Prophecy Document
THE COMPLETE END-TIMES PROPHECY STUDY
ALL SCRIPTURE INTERPRETED BY SCRIPTURE - EVERY VERSE
INCLUDED
Using Scripture's Own Definitions and the Sequential Trigger Mechanism
INTRODUCTION: THE LENS WE VIEW THROUGH
The Principle: Let the Bible interpret the Bible. Use Scripture's own words and definitions. Do not
impose external meaning—extract the meaning Scripture itself provides through cross-reference and
parallel passage.
The Framework: - Daniel provides the TIMELINE (kingdoms, the little horn, the end times) - 1 & 2
Thessalonians provide the TRIGGER SIGNAL ("Peace and Safety" = the warning moment) -
Revelation provides the MECHANISM (how the system operates, the mark, the judgments) - The
Other Prophets provide CONFIRMATION and DETAIL
The Window: - Israel became a nation: 1948 - A biblical generation: 70-80 years (Psalm 90:10) -
Prophetic window: 1948 + 70-80 = 2017-2027 - We are in 2026. The window is closing.
PART ONE: THE KINGDOMS FRAMEWORK - DANIEL'S
TIMELINE


---

Daniel 2: The Statue and the Four Kingdoms
Daniel 2:31-35 - Nebuchadnezzar's Dream (The Statue):
"Thou, O king, sawest, and behold a great image. This great image, whose brightness was excellent,
stood before thee; and the form thereof was terrible. This image's head was of fine gold, his breast and
his arms of silver, his belly and his thighs of brass, His legs of iron, his feet part of iron and part of clay.
Thou sawest till that a stone was cut out without hands, which smote the image upon his feet that were
of iron and clay, and brake them to pieces."
Definition of the Kingdoms (Daniel 2:36-43):
"Thou art the head of gold. And after thee shall arise another kingdom inferior to thee, and another third
kingdom of brass, which shall bear rule over all the earth. And the fourth kingdom shall be strong as
iron: forasmuch as iron breaketh in pieces and subdueth all things... And whereas thou sawest the feet
and toes, part of potters' clay, and part of iron, the kingdom shall be divided; but there shall be in it of
the strength of the iron, forasmuch as thou sawest the iron mixed with miry clay. And as the toes of the
feet were part of iron, and part of clay, so the kingdom shall be partly strong, and partly broken."
Scripture's Definition of "Iron and Clay Mixed":
"And whereas thou sawest iron mixed with miry clay, they shall mingle themselves with the seed of
men: but they shall not cleave one to another, even as iron is not mixed with clay" (Daniel 2:43).
Translation: The final kingdom (iron and clay feet) is characterized by: - Division - Weakness (cannot
hold together) - Multiple kingdoms trying to unite but failing - From the Roman Empire forward
The End of All Kingdoms (Daniel 2:44-45):
"And in the days of these kings shall the God of heaven set up a kingdom, which shall never be
destroyed: and the kingdom shall not be left to other people, but it shall break in pieces and consume all
these kingdoms, and it shall stand for ever."
Daniel 7: The Four Beasts (Parallel to the Four Kingdoms)
Daniel 7:1-8 - The Four Beasts:
"I saw in the night visions, and behold four great beasts came up from the sea... The first was like a
lion... And behold another beast, a second, like to a bear... After this I beheld, and lo another, like a
leopard, which had upon the back of it four wings... After this I saw in the night visions, and behold a
fourth beast, dreadful and terrible, and strong exceedingly; and it had great iron teeth... And I
considered the horns, and, behold, there came up among them another little horn."
The Identity of the Beasts (Daniel 7:17-23):


---

"These great beasts, which are four, are four kings, which shall arise out of the earth... The fourth beast
shall be the fourth kingdom upon earth, which shall be diverse from all kingdoms, and shall devour the
whole earth, and shall tread it down, and break it in pieces. And the ten horns out of this kingdom are
ten kings that shall arise: and another shall rise after them; and he shall be diverse from the first, and he
shall subdue three kings."
The Four Kingdoms Identified by Scripture: 1. Lion = Babylon (Daniel 2:38) 2. Bear = Medo-Persia
(Daniel 8:20) 3. Leopard = Greece (Daniel 8:21) 4. Fourth Beast = Rome (by elimination and historical
confirmation)
Daniel 7: The Little Horn (The Power That Speaks Great Words)
Daniel 7:8 - The Little Horn Appears:
"I considered the horns, and, behold, there came up among them another little horn, before whom there
were three of the first horns plucked up by the roots: and, behold, in this horn were eyes like the eyes of
a man, and a mouth speaking great things."
Daniel 7:24-25 - Scripture's Definition of the Little Horn:
"And the ten horns out of this kingdom are ten kings that shall arise: and another shall rise after them;
and he shall be diverse from the first, and he shall subdue three kings. And he shall speak great words
against the most High, and shall wear out the saints of the most High, and think to change times and
laws: and they shall be given into his hand until a time and times and the dividing of time."
What the Little Horn Does (Scripture's Definition):
1. Speaks great words AGAINST the Most High = Blasphemy 2. Wears out the saints =

from Saturday to Sunday) 4. Given dominion for "time, times, and dividing of time" = 1,260 years
(from ~5th century to ~17th century and beyond as spiritual influence)
Who is This? The Papal System - emerges from Rome's divisions, claims religious authority above
God, persecuted Christians, changed the Sabbath command.
Daniel 8: The Little Horn Revisited (The End Times Version)
Daniel 8:9-11 - Another Little Horn Vision:
"And out of one of them came forth a little horn, which waxed exceeding great, toward the south, and
toward the east, and toward the pleasant land. And it waxed great, even to the host of heaven; and it cast
down some of the host and of the stars to the ground, and stamped upon them. Yea, he magnified
himself even to the prince of the host, and by him the daily sacrifice was taken away, and the place of
the sanctuary was cast down."


---

Daniel 8:13-14 - The Prophecy's Duration:
"Then I heard one saint speaking, and another saint said unto that certain saint which spake, How long
shall be the vision concerning the daily sacrifice, and the transgression of desolation, to give both the
sanctuary and the host to be trodden under foot? And he said unto me, Unto two thousand and three
hundred days; then shall the sanctuary be cleansed."
Meaning: A period of desolation, then restoration (the final events).
Daniel 9: The Seventy Weeks and the Abomination of Desolation
Daniel 9:24 - The Scope of the Prophecy:
"Seventy weeks are determined upon thy people and upon thy holy city, to finish the transgression, and
to make an end of sins, and to make reconciliation for iniquity, and to bring in everlasting

"Know therefore and understand, that from the going forth of the commandment to restore and to build

shall come shall destroy the city and the sanctuary."
Daniel 9:27 - THE CRITICAL VERSE FOR THE END TIMES:
"And he shall confirm the covenant with many for one week: and in the midst of the week he shall
cause the sacrifice and the oblation to cease, and for the overspreading of abominations he shall make it
desolate, even until the consummation, and that determined shall be poured upon the desolate."
Scripture's Definition of "Abomination that Maketh Desolate":
In Daniel 12:11: "And from the time that the daily sacrifice shall be taken away, and the abomination
that maketh desolate set up, there shall be a thousand two hundred and ninety days."
This prophecy concerns the final period - the "abomination of desolation" is SET UP in the end times,
triggering the countdown to Christ's return.
Daniel 10:14 - "The Latter Days"
"Now I am come to make thee understand what shall befall thy people in the latter days: for yet the
vision is for many days."

Daniel 12: The Sealing Until the Time of the End

Implication: When we are in the time of the end, those who follow Scripture carefully WILL

PART TWO: THE TRIGGER SIGNAL - 1 THESSALONIANS 5
1 Thessalonians 5:1-3 - THE KEY SIGNAL
1 Thessalonians 5:1-2 - Introduction:
"But of the times and the seasons, brethren, ye have no need that I write unto you. For yourselves know
perfectly that the day of the Lord so cometh as a thief in the night."
1 Thessalonians 5:3 - THE TRIGGER VERSE:
"For when they shall say, Peace and safety; then sudden destruction cometh upon them, as travail upon
a woman with child; and they shall not escape."
Scripture's Definition of "Peace and Safety":
This is NOT referring to genuine peace or safety. It is a FALSE declaration by the world system. When
world leaders declare they have achieved "peace," that is when judgment comes.
The Imagery: "Travail upon a woman with child"
Paul is using the EXACT image from Revelation 12:2 - the woman in labor. This is NOT coincidental.
The Scripture interprets itself:


---

Revelation 12:2: "And she being with child cried, travailing in birth, and pained to be delivered."
Connection: The "Peace and Safety" moment marks the beginning of the FINAL LABOR PAINS of
human history. Just as labor pains accelerate and intensify until delivery, the end-times events
accelerate and intensify until Christ's return.
Historical Fulfillment in 2026

This is the fulfillment of 1 Thessalonians 5:3 in real time.

What This Means (Scripture's Own Definition):

Matthew 24:3-14 - The Warning and the Beginning of Sorrows
Matthew 24:3 - The Question Asked:

shall these things be? and what shall be the sign of thy coming, and of the end of the world?"
Matthew 24:4 - Jesus's First Warning:
"Take heed that no man deceive you."
The very first thing Jesus says about the end times is: DECEPTION will be the primary weapon.
Matthew 24:5-6 - False Christs and Wars:
"For many shall come in my name, saying, I am Christ; and shall deceive many. And ye shall hear of

Definition: - Many false christs will appear - Wars and rumors of wars will abound - But these are

Matthew 24:7-8 - The Beginning of Sorrows:
"For nation shall rise against nation, and kingdom against kingdom: and there shall be famines, and

Jesus Defines "Beginning of Sorrows" as: - Nations rising against nations - Famines - Pestilences -
Earthquakes in various places
Matthew 24:9-14 - Persecution and the Gospel Preached:
"Then shall they deliver you up to be afflicted, and shall kill you: and ye shall hated of all nations for
my name's sake. And then shall many be offended, and shall betray one another, and shall hate one
another. And many false prophets shall rise, and shall deceive many. And because iniquity shall
abound, the love of many shall wax cold. But he that shall endure unto the end, the same shall be saved.
And this gospel of the kingdom shall be preached in all the world for a witness unto all nations; and
then shall the end come."
Jesus Defines the End-Time Persecution: - Believers delivered up to be afflicted and killed - Hatred

increasing) - Love growing cold - The faithful MUST ENDURE - The gospel must be preached to ALL

Jesus's Own Definition: He REFERS BACK TO DANIEL - letting Daniel interpret it.
Matthew 24:16-20 - The Command:
"Then let them which be in Judaea flee into the mountains: Let him which is on the housetop not come
down to take any thing out of his house: Neither let him which is in the field return back to take his
clothes. But pray ye that your flight be not in the winter, neither on the sabbath day."
Important Detail: Jesus says pray that flight be not on the SABBATH day. This shows the Sabbath is
still binding in the end times.
Matthew 24:21-22 - Great Tribulation:
"For then shall be great tribulation, such as was not since the beginning of the world to this time, no,

Jesus Defines "Great Tribulation": - Greater than any suffering in history - Would kill ALL FLESH

Matthew 24:23-27 - False Christs and the True Coming

"Then if any man shall say unto you, Lo, here is Christ, or there; believe it not. For there shall arise
false Christs, and false prophets, and shall shew great signs and wonders; insomuch that, if it were

desert; go not forth: behold, he is in the secret chambers; believe it not."
Matthew 24:27 - The True Coming is Unmistakable:
"For as the lightning cometh out of the east, and shineth even unto the west; so shall also the coming of

---

Revelation 12: The Woman in Travail
